Patient had pan scan and trauma labs trauma labs negative pan scan negative for intrathoracic, intra-abdominal or intracranial hemorrhage. Patient able to tolerate p.o. ambulate subsequently discharged.

Studebaker Rm9 *

Patient: WILLIAMS, ASHLEE KANDICE MRN: T003082849 FIN: T[PHONE-4] Age: 20 years Sex: Female DOB: 12/1/2002

Associated Diagnoses: MVC (motor vehicle collision); Arm pain

Author: STUDEBAKER, HAELY A, MD-EMR

History of Present Illness

Patient is a 20-year-old female with a history of asthma, anxiety, depression, Bipolar 1, and panic attacks who presents as the unrestrained passenger. Per EMS, the patient was going 40-50mph when they got into the accident. Patient reports hitting her head on the airbags, causing her to loss consciousness.

Attending: Dr. Kuzel EMS notification Prior to Arrival: Yes Initial Vitals: See nurse;s note Primary survey: Airway self-maintained. Breathing spontaneously, equal BS, bilat chest rise. Normal sinus rhythm on monitor, IVs obtained. Secondary survey per documented exam. Imaging results: - Chest X-ray shows no obvious rib fractures, no hemothorax or pneumothorax as interpreted by me FAST results: Negative Consults: none Initial Impression: MVA Disposition: To CT

Critical care time excluding procedure time: < 20 min

Room 9 Course:

21:24 Patient transferred onto bed

21:25 Vitals obtained BP118/84

21:26 97.9 temperature, FAST

21:27 Glucose 96

21:28 Warm LR started, pt transferred to CT

Differential includes fracture, laceration, abrasion, vascular injury, intracranial injury, intrathoracic injury, intraabdominal injury, spinal fracture, spinal cord injury, musculoskeletal pain, muscle spasm.

All labs and images independently reviewed and interpreted

CT of the head showed no intracranial bleeding, no intrathoracic or intra-abdominal bleeding, no free air, x-ray of the humerus shows no fracture. CT C, T, L-spine showed no fractures. | cleared the patient c-collar and she was able to move her head in all directions without any pain. Patient's pain was

well controlled while she was here in the department. Results from today’s work-up were discussed with the patient and all questions were answered. At this time the patient is stable for discharge home. Patient states they feel comfortable being discharged home. | have advised the patient that is important follow-up with their PCP in the next 2 to 3 days. Patient is agreeable to discharge plan and verbalizes understanding of return precautions.

| have discussed with the patient that they are likely to be increasingly sore over the next 2 to 3 days. They will be discharged with a prescription for ibuprofen and Skelaxin. | have advised to alternate Tylenol and ibuprofen every 3-4 hours and to add in the Skelaxin for additional pain control needed. | informed the patient that the maximum daily intake of tylenol is 4000 mg over a 24 hour period. | have discussed with the pt that while Skelaxin is generally less sedating than other muscle relaxers, the pt should avoid driving or operating heavy machinery while on this medication. | have also recommended that the pt not work while taking Skelaxin unless first disclosing the information to their boss with approval. Patient receptive to the information and agreeable. All questions regarding the prescriptions were answered.

Physical Examination

Vital Signs Skin: abrasion with bruising to right upper arm. Eye: Extraocular movements are intact. Cardiovascular: Regular rate and rhythm, 2+ radial and DP pulse. Chest wall: No tenderness. Musculoskeletal: tender over right upper arm. Respiratory: Respirations are non-labored. Genitourinary Gastrointestinal: Nontender, Non distended. Psychiatric: Cooperative. General: No acute distress.

Impression and Plan Diagnosis MVC (motor vehicle collision) - Discharge, Medical MVC (motor vehicle collision) - Discharge, Medical Arm pain - Discharge, Medical

Plan Prescriptions: Prescription Writer Pharmacy: Skelaxin 800 mg oral tablet (Prescribe): 800 mg = 1 Tab, Oral, TID, for 7 Day(s), 21 Tab, 0 Refill(s) ibuprofen 600 mg oral tablet (Prescribe): 600 mg = 1 Tab, Oral, Q8H, for 30 Day(s), 90 Tab, 0 Refill(s) Tylenol 325 mg oral capsule (Prescribe): 650 mg = 2 Cap, Oral, TID, for 30 Day(s), PRN: as needed for pain, 180 Cap, 0 Refill(s). Patient was given the following educational materials: Musculoskeletal Pain, Motor Vehicle Collision Injury, Adult, Easy-to-Read, Motor Vehicle Collision Injury, Adult, Easy-to-Read, Musculoskeletal Pain.

Follow up with: Primary Care Provider Within 2 to 3 days We had the pleasure of evaluating you in the Emergency Department today in an attempt to rule out any life threatening, emergent conditions based on the medical issue that you verbalized. Unforunately, it is often difficult to make a final diagnosis in the Emergency Department. It is not a comprehensive evaluation and does not guarantee that you do not have a medical issue that should be addressed, therefore, it is important you follow up with your primary care physician and any recommended specalist(s) for further evaluation. Please take all medications as prescribed.

If your condition worsens, or you experience any concerning symptoms, such as: passing out, high fevers, chest pain, shortness of air, inability to tolerate food or liquids, abdominal pain, weakness / numbness, or any other concerning symptoms please return to the Emergency Department.

If you have any questions or concerns about your visit today, please call: [PHONE-7]. If you do not have a primary medical doctor, feel free to refer to the list below.

As part of your treatment plan, your provider may have prescribed a limited course of a controlled substance. This medication may be given to help people with moderate or severe pain or for other medical conditions, but there are risks involved with treatment. Common side effects may include nausea, constipation, drowsiness, sweating, itching, dry mouth, and rash. More serious side effects may include cognitive and motor impairment, like problems with thinking, concentrating, alertness, and movement (e.g. slowed reflexes), and driving and operating heavy machinery can be dangerous. It is important for you to talk to your provider if you have these side effects or questions. These controlled substances can produce physical dependence and be habit-forming if taken for an extended period of time, which means that the body has gotten used to them and may experience withdrawal symptoms, if they are abruptly stopped. Education Materials

Motor Vehicle Collision Injury, Adult

After a car accident (motor vehicle collision), it is common to have injuries to your head, face, arms, and body. These injuries may include:

° Cuts. ° Burns. ° Bruises.

. Sore muscles or a stretch or tear in a muscle (strain). ° Headaches.

You may feel stiff and sore for the first several hours. You may feel worse after waking up the first morning after the accident. These injuries often feel worse for the first 24-48 hours. After that, you will usually begin to get better with each day. How quickly you get better often depends on:

. How bad the accident was.

° How many injuries you have.

° Where your injuries are.

° What types of injuries you have. . If you were wearing a seat belt. ° If your airbag was used.

A head injury may result in a concussion. This is a type of brain injury that can have serious effects. If you have a concussion, you should rest as told by your doctor. You must be very careful to avoid having a second concussion.

Follow these instructions at home: Medicines

° Take over-the-counter and prescription medicines only as told by your doctor.

° If you were prescribed antibiotic medicine, take or apply it as told by your doctor. Do not stop using the antibiotic even if your condition gets better.

If you have a wound or a burn:

Normal Infected wound wound

° Clean your wound or burn as told by your doctor.

—46 Wash it with mild soap and water.

—46 Rinse it with water to get all the soap off.

—46 Pat it dry with a clean towel. Do not rub it.

—46 If you were told to put an ointment or cream on the wound, do so as told by your doctor.

° Follow instructions from your doctor about how to take care of your wound or burn. Make sure you:

—46 Know when and how to change or remove your bandage (dressing).

—46 Always wash your hands with soap and water before and after you change your bandage. If you cannot use soap and water, use hand sanitizer.

—46 Leave stitches (sutures), skin glue, or skin tape (adhesive) strips in place, if you have these. They may need to stay in place for 2 weeks or longer. If tape strips get loose and curl up, you may trim the loose edges. Do not remove tape strips completely unless your doctor says it is okay.

. Do not:

—46 Scratch or pick at the wound or burn.

—46 Break any blisters you may have.

—46 Peel any skin.

° Avoid getting sun on your wound or burn. ° Raise (elevate) the wound or burn above the level of your heart while you are sitting or lying down. If you have a wound or burn on your face, you may want to sleep with your head raised. You may do this by putting an extra pillow under your head. ° Check your wound or burn every day for signs of infection. Check for: —46 More redness, swelling, or pain. —46 More fluid or blood.

Musculoskeletal pain refers to aches and pains in your bones, joints, muscles, and the tissues that surround them. This pain can occur

Musculoskeletal Pain

in any part of the body. It can last for a short time (acute) or a long time (chronic).

A physical exam, lab tests, and imaging studies may be done to find the cause of your musculoskeletal pain.

Follow these instructions at home:

Lifestyle

Try to control or lower your stress levels. Stress increases muscle tension and can worsen musculoskeletal pain. It is important to recognize when you are anxious or stressed and learn ways to manage it. This may include:

—46 Meditation or yoga.

—46 Cognitive or behavioral therapy.

—46 Acupuncture or massage therapy.

You may continue all activities unless the activities cause more pain. When the pain gets better, slowly resume your normal activities. Gradually increase the intensity and duration of your activities or exercise.

Managing pain, stiffness, and swelling

Treatment may include medicines for pain and inflammation that are taken by mouth or applied to the skin. Take

over-the-counter and prescription medicines only as told by your health care provider.

When your pain is severe, bed rest may be helpful. Lie or sit in any position that is comfortable, but get out of bed and walk

around at least every couple of hours.

If directed, apply heat to the affected area as often as told by your health care provider. Use the heat source that your health

care provider recommends, such as a moist heat pack or a heating pad.

—46 Place a towel between your skin and the heat source.

—46 Leave the heat on for 20-30 minutes.

—46 Remove the heat if your skin turns bright red. This is especially important if you are unable to feel pain, heat, or cold. You may have a greater risk of getting burned.

If directed, put ice on the painful area. To do this:

—46 Put ice in a plastic bag.

° Musculoskeletal pain refers to aches and pains in your bones, joints, muscles, and the tissues that surround them.

° This pain can occur in any part of the body.

° Your health care provider may recommend that you see a physical therapist. This person can help you come up with a safe exercise program. Do any exercises as told by your physical therapist.

° Lower your stress level. Stress can worsen musculoskeletal pain. Ways to lower stress may include meditation, yoga, cognitive or behavioral therapy, acupuncture, and massage therapy.

Cigarette Smoking

The facts are clear, cigarette smoking will shorten your life. Smoking can cause many illnesses along the way. As a healthcare provider, we recommend that you stop smoking. Assistance with quitting is available by contacting 1-800-QUIT-NOW. This is a free resource providing counseling, support, and referral. Or you may contact your personal physician.

988 Suicide & Crisis Lifeline: 988 The 988 Suicide & Crisis Lifeline is a national network of local crisis centers that provides free and confidential emotional support to people in suicidal crisis or emotional distress 24 hours a day, 7 days a week.

Don't Wait! Stop a Heart Attack Before It Starts

What is a heart attack?

A heart attack is damage or death to a part of the heart from severely decreased or lack of blood flow to the heart. Over time, arteries can become narrow from the buildup of fat and cholesterol, which is called plaque. The plaque can rupture causing a blood clot to form. When the blood clot forms, the artery can become severely narrowed or completely blocked, causing a heart attack.

¢ Heart attack is the leading cause of death in the United States. * 85% of muscle damage occurs within the first 2 hours.

* Delay in the recognition of heart attack symptoms increases the chances of death.

Know the early symptoms of a heart attack:

Feeling of Pain that travels Nausea "fullness" in Jaw Pain down one or chest both arms . . Chest pressure, Fatigue/being Anxiety Back Pain squeezing, or discomfort Shortness of Sweating, or a A ecling oF breath cold sweat impending doom

There are unusual signs of heart attack, too! Women, the elderly, and diabetics may present with atypical symptoms:

Risk Factors for a Heart Attack

Some heart disease risk factors, such as age and family, cannot be changed. Others, like smoking and lack of exercise, can be changed.

Smoking High Cholesterol Blood Pressure Family History Obesity Age

Gender (Males are . .

at higher risk) Lack of Exercise Diabetes

Diet Stress Excessive Alcohol

Intake

If you or someone you know is experiencing the signs and symptoms of a heart attack, DON'T DELAY. Call 9-1-1 immediately and seek help.

If someone collapses, perform CPR!

Do not attempt to drive if you are having symptoms of heart attack.

Why Hands-Only CPR?

* Hands-Only CPR has been shown to be as effective as conventional CPR for cardiac arrests that occur outside of a hospital.

* Survival depends on immediately receiving CPR from someone nearby.

How do you perform Hands-Only CPR? There are two easy steps:

* 1. Call 9-1-1 if you see a teen or adult collapse

¢ 2. Push hard and fast in the center of the chest at a beat of 100 beats per minute

Save a life!

4 WAYS TO GET AHEAD OF SEPSIS SEPSIS is a MEDICAL EMERGENCY. Time Matters!

Infections put you and your family at risk for a life-threatening condition called sepsis.

* Sepsis is the body's extreme response to an infection. It is life-threatening, and without timely treatment, sepsis can rapidly lead to tissue damage, organ failure, and death. Sepsis happens when an infection you already have-in your skin, lungs, urinary tract or somewhere else-riggers a chain reaction throughout your body.

PREVENT * Take good care of INFECTIONS chronic conditions.

Patient: WILLIAMS, ASHLEE KANDICE DOB/Age/Sex: 12/1/2002 20 years Female MRN: [PHONE-299] Account #: T[PHONE-298] Coagulation

Collected Date 8/29/2023 Collected Time 22:07 EDT

Procedure Units Ref Range PT 10.5#'R81 Second(s) [9.7-11.5] INR 1.0 #R) PTT 23.7*R1 ~=Second(s) [23.3-33.2] Interpretive Data #1: PT

When using the PT to screen for a coagulopathy, please refer to the PT reference

range to evaluate results. #2: INR To monitor warfarin, the INR calculated from the PT is used, according to current

published guidelines: *Most indications, moderate intensity INR (2.0-3.0) is effective.

*Patients with recurrent thromboembolic events with a therapeutic INR as above, or other additional risk factors for thromboembolic events, high intensity INR (2.5-3.5) is recommended.

*Optimal target range for the INR is not likely to be the same for all indications, and lower INR targets may be prudent for patients at very high risk of bleeding.

The INR is used to manage patients on warfarin, and thus is not compared to a "normal" INR range. The validity of the INR in other conditions of impaired coagulation has not been fully evaluated, and the PT recorded in seconds is recommended in these instances. Ref: CHEST June 2008 supplement.

#3: PTT

To screen for coagulaopathy, refer to reference range in seconds.

To monitor intravenous unfractionated heparin, the therapeutic aPTT range has been determined by this laboratory to be 55.1 - 66.4 seconds. Patients who require high doses of heparin to achieve a therapeutic aPTT, or in patients with a prolonged baseline aPTT (ie lupus anticoagulant), it is reasonable to adjust heparin doses based on anti Xa levels (unfractionated heparin assay) to achieve a level of 0.3 - 0.7 IU/ml. The aPTT is also used to monitor direct thrombin inhibitors as per pharmacy protocols.

The Law: There |. a federal law called the Health Insurance Portability and Accountability Act of 1996 (“HIPAA”). This law requires UofL Health to protect the privacy and security of its patients’ treatment, contact, and financial inforn ation. Taken together, this information is called your “Health Information”. There are also other federal and/o’ state laws that require UofL Health to take additional steps to protect certain categories of Health Information including, but not limited to, Health Information about behavioral or mental health; developmental disa »ilities; treatment for substance abuse (alcohol and/or drugs) disorders; genetic testing and counseling; HIV/AIL S; sexual assault/ abuse; sexually transmitted illnesses; pregnancy; birth control; domestic abuse of an adult w ‘h a disability; child abuse and neglect.

Oswestry Low Back Pain Scaic L~

Please rate the severity of your pain by circling a number below:

No pain 0 1

Name \ssoocst Smee

2 4.8 4 B89

aes ee es Unbearable pain

Date QW DX

instructions: Please circle the ONE NUMBER in each section which most closely describes your problem.

Section 1 — Pain Intensity

0. The pain comes and goes and is very mild.

4. The pain is mild and does not vary much.

2. The pain comes and goes and is moderate.

3. The pain is moderate and does not vary much. 4. The pain comes and goes and is severe.

5. The pain is severe and does not vary much.

Section 2 — Personal Care (Washing, Dressing, etc.)

0. | would not have to change my way of washing or dressing in order to avoid pain.

4. | do not normally change my way of washing or dressing even though it causes some pain.

2. Washing and dressing increase the pain but | manage not to change my way of doing it.

3. Washing and dressing increase the pain and | find it necessary to change my way of doing it.

4. Because of the pain | am unable to do some washing and dressing without help.

5. Because of the pain | am unable to do any washing and dressing without help.

Section 3 — Lifting

_|can lift heavy weights without extra pain.

_ | can lift heavy weights but it gives extra pain.

. Pain prevents me lifting heavy weights off the floor.

. Pain prevents me lifting heavy weights off the floor, but | can manage if they are conveniently positioned, e.g., on a table.

. Pain prevents me lifting heavy weights but | can manage light to medium weights if they are conveniently positioned.

5. | can only lift very light weights at most.

WON oO

a

Section 4 — Walking

0. | have no pain on walking.

. [have some pain on walking but it does not increase with distance.

2. | cannot walk more than 1 mile without increasing pain.

3. | cannot walk more than % mile without increasing pain.

4. | cannot walk more than % mile without increasing pain.

5. | cannot walk at all without increasing pain.

is

Section 5 — Sitting

0. | can sit in any chair as long as | like.

1. | can sit only in my favorite chair as long as | like.

2. Pain prevents me from sitting more than 1 hour.

3. Pain prevents me from sitting more than % hour.

4. Pain prevents me from sitting more than 10 minutes. 5. | avoid sitting because it increases pain immediately.

Section 6 - Standing

_ | can stand as long as | want without pain.

. | have some pain on standing but it does not increase with time.

_ | cannot stand for longer than 1 hour without increasing pain.

. | cannot stand for longer than % hour without increasing pain.

_ | cannot stand for longer than 10 minutes without increasing pain. . | avoid standing because it increases the pain immediately.

OhwWN oO

Section 7 — Sleeping

0. | get no pain in bed.

1. | get pain in bed but it does not prevent me from sleeping well.

2. Because of pain my normal nights sleep is reduced by less than one-quarter.

3. Because of pain my normal nights sleep is reduced by less than one-half.

4. Because of pain my normal nights sleep is reduced by less than three-quarters.

5. Pain prevents me from sleeping at all.

Section 8 - Social Life

0. My social life is normal and gives me no pain.

1. My social life is normal but it increases the degree of pain.

2. Pain has no significant effect on my social life apart from limiting my more energetic interests, e.g., dancing, etc.

3. Pain has restricted my social life and | do not go out very often.

4. Pain has restricted my social life to my home.

5. | have hardly any social life because of the pain.

Section 9 — Traveling

0. | get no pain when traveling.

1. | get some pain when traveling but none of my usual forms of travel make it any worse.

2. | get extra pain while traveling but it does not compel me to seek alternate forms of travel.

3. | get extra pain while traveling which compels to seek alternative forms of travel.

4. Pain restricts me to short necessary journeys under % hour.

5. Pain restricts all forms of travel.

Section 10 ~ Changing Degree of Pain

. My pain is rapidly getting better.

. My pain fluctuates but is definitely getting better.

. My pain seems to be getting better but improvement is slow. . My pain is neither getting better or worse.

. My pain is gradually worsening.

. My pain is rapidly worsening.

ObhWN—-O

TOTAL

Kentucky Pain Associates, PLLC 222 South 1° Street, Suite 300 Louisville, KY 40202

PATIENT NAME: Ashlee Williams DATE OF SERVICE: [DOB-325] DATE OF INJURY: [DOB-326] PAGE: 1 of 7

PRACTITIONER INITIAL EVALUATION

HISTORY OF PRESENT INJURY: Patient is a 20-year-old female, who was the unrestrained front-seat passenger of a vehicle involved in a motor vehicle accident. The vehicle was hit on the passenger side and was totaled. The air bag deployed. Police were present at the scene. Patient was seen by the emergency room doctor at University of Louisville Hospital. She was taken to the ER by ambulance. Medical records regarding this accident have been ordered from the originating physician. She has taken Ibuprofen to treat her pain with no relief. She has been taking Naproxen to treat her pain with no relief. She has experienced severe right arm pain, rated as 9 out of 10, severe headache pain, rated as 8 out of 10, severe right upper leg pain, rated as 7 out of 10, severe mid/upper back pain, rated as 8 out of 10, severe neck pain, rated as 8 out of 10, severe right shoulder pain, rated as 9 out of 10, right ribs pain, described as severe, rated as 8 out of 10. Patient did not have pain right before this accident happened.

Patient describes headaches as intermittent, pressure, vise-like lasting several hours and resolving on their own. She does have a history of anxiety and endorses an increased level of anxiety accompanied by intermittent memory loss and being easily irritated since the MVC. She endorses severe right shoulder pain with numbness and tingling in the right hand. She endorses mid/upper back pain without radicular symptoms. She endorses low back pain with radicular symptoms to the right lower extremity. She endorses mid sternal pain, right anterior chest wall pain, right lateral chest pain and right hip pain. States pain is worse with all range of motion, prolonged sitting, standing and transitioning form the sitting to the standing position. ImPACT test in 1 week. Patient informed and verbalized understanding.

The patient denies any previous headaches, neck pain, referred fight trapezius pain, right shoulder pain, mid sternum pain, right chest wall pain, right lateral chest wall pain, mid/upper back pain, low back pain, right hip pain, radicular symptoms, increased anxiety prior to the current MVC (deny any previous pain complaint for regions not injured in previous injury).

The patient was educated on and verbalized understanding of the purpose and goals of pain management. Motor vehicle collision speed was greater than 17 MPH and experienced moderate or more damage.

Patient suffered quick or violent movements to the neck and/or body. Patient suffered a blow to

the head. Patient states she did lose consciousness. She was unconscious for approximately two minutes. Patient states loss of consciousness was witnessed.

Kentucky Pain Associates, PLLC 222 South 1° Street, Suite 300 Louisville, KY 40202

PATIENT NAME: Ashlee Williams DATE OF SERVICE: [DOB-327] DATE OF INJURY: [DOB-328] PAGE: 2 of 7

An Acute Concussion Evaluation (ACE - Physician/Clinician Office Version) was administered on the patient today to confirm the suspicion of a traumatic brain injury/concussion. The ACE is an evidence-based tool that assists providers in the assessment and diagnosis of concussions and traumatic brain injuries. The patient states that since the motor vehicle accident, she has experienced the following brain injury related symptoms: headache, irritability, nausea, sadness, vomiting, more emotional, nervousness, dizziness, fatigue (tired), sensitivity to light, sleeping less than usual, sensitivity to noise, numbness/tingling, trouble falling asleep, feeling mentally foggy, feeling slowed down, difficulty concentrating, difficulty remembering. Results were reviewed with the patient and scanned into our system.

IMAGING: Patient has had X-Ray, CT scan done previously. She brought her images to today's appointment. 8/29/2023 CT results revealed the following: Head: no acute intracranial abnormality or facture. Cervical Spine: no acute fracture, Chest: no evidence of acute traumatic injury, Abdomen/Pelvis: no traumatic visceral injury, Thoracic Spine: no acute fracture or subluxation, Right Humerus: no acute fracture or dislocation, Lumbar Spine: no acute fracture or subluxation.

WORK AND/OR SCHOOL STATUS: Patient was working prior to the accident. She is currently working full time normal duty. She is performing duties under duress. She is working out of necessity. Patient is employed as a lash tech.

MEDICAL HISTORY: Patient has a history of Seizures. Patient states that she is not pregnant.

PSYCHIATRIC HISTORY: Patient has a history of psychiatric problems, specifically Depression, Bipolar Disorder.

SURGICAL HISTORY: Patient has a history of surgery that includes tonsillectomy. ALLERGIES: No known medical allergies. MEDICATIONS: Patient takes Keppra 1000mg. She does not use any blood thinners.

SOCIAL HISTORY: Patient smokes vapes. Patient denies drinking alcohol. Patient denies the use of illegal drugs.

FAMILY HISTORY: Patient denies any significant family medical history. REVIEW OF SYSTEMS: Review of systems is positive for headaches, trouble sleeping due to

pain, dizziness, irritability, anxiety, nausea/vomiting, lungs/trouble breathing. Patient denies all other physical problems except for those listed in the history of present injury.

Pain Medication is short-term, temporary, and not the primary treatment. Pain Medication is a Supplement to a multi-modal approach that includes other treatment options such as non-opioid based medications and therapy. Based on professional judgment, this multi- modal approach is believed to be the best treatment option at this time. Short-term and temporary.

The Patient will be evaluated per the frequency indicated below to monitor all medications and treatment(s) and to determine and document interval improvement and response to therapy/treatment.

Patient has been instructed not to drive or operate any machinery while taking these medications. Patient's KASPER report was reviewed and a copy added to the chart.

2. Therapy: The patient states that she is receiving rehabilitation therapy at this time. I agree with Dr. Sears's treatment plan for this patient that initially consists of passive modalities for pain control and transitions into a more active rehabilitation treatment plan as the patient progresses, barring any injury exacerbations or setbacks. I have instructed the patient to return to her physician to continue her therapeutic modalities and will periodically check in with the physician's updated treatment plan to see patient's rehabilitation progress. The patient has been going to therapy 4 days per week.
